<summary>🤖 Subagent (spark): Fix governance timing</summary>

**Input:**

**Agent:** `spark` | **Description:** Fix governance timing  

Fix lib/governance.ts for timing side-channel in verifyPassword.  

Read the file first: /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/governance.ts  

The issue: verifyPassword() returns false immediately when no password hash is set, creating a timing difference that reveals whether governance has a password.  

Fix: When no hash is set, run a dummy bcrypt comparison against a static hash so the timing is consistent:  

```typescript
export function verifyPassword(password: string): boolean {
  const config = loadGovernance()
  if (!config.passwordHash) {
    // Constant-time defense: run bcrypt even when no password is set
    // to prevent timing side-channel that reveals password existence
    bcrypt.compareSync(password, '$2a$12$000000000000000000000000000000000000000000')
    return false
  }
  return bcrypt.compareSync(password, config.passwordHash)
}
```

Use a valid bcrypt hash format for the dummy (any static bcrypt hash will do). Add a comment explaining why.

This is a large file (~1300 lines). Search for `gw_list` to find the relevant section.

gw_list="${gw_list}"$'\n'"- ${gw_display}"
```

    23→function tasksFilePath(teamId: string): string {

    25→  if (!/^[0-9a-f-]{36}$/i.test(teamId)) throw new Error('Invalid team ID')  
    26→  // Defense-in-depth: use basename to strip any directory components  
    27→  return path.join(TEAMS_DIR, path.basename(`tasks-${teamId}.json`))

    30→export function loadTasks(teamId: string): Task[] {

    39→    return Array.isArray(parsed.tasks) ? parsed.tasks : []  
    40→  } catch (error) {  
    41→    console.error(`Failed to load tasks for team ${teamId}:`, error)  
    42→    return []  
    43→  }

   200→  function hasCycle(currentId: string): boolean {  
   201→    if (currentId === taskId) return true  
   202→    if (visited.has(currentId)) return false  
   203→    visited.add(currentId)  
   204→  
   205→    const task = tasks.find(t => t.id === currentId)  
   206→    if (!task) return false  
   207→  
   208→    // Check what this task blocks (tasks that depend on it)  
   209→    const blockers = tasks.filter(t => t.blockedBy.includes(currentId))  
   210→    return blockers.some(b => hasCycle(b.id))  
   211→  }  
   212→  
   213→  return hasCycle(dependencyId)  
   214→}

```
export function createTask(data: {
  teamId: string
  subject: string
  description?: string
  assigneeAgentId?: string | null
  blockedBy?: string[]
  priority?: number
}): Task {
  const tasks = loadTasks(data.teamId)
  const now = new Date().toISOString()

  const task: Task = {
    id: uuidv4(),
    teamId: data.teamId,
    subject: data.subject,
    description: data.description,
    status: 'pending',
    assigneeAgentId: data.assigneeAgentId || null,
    blockedBy: data.blockedBy || [],
    priority: data.priority,
    createdAt: now,
    updatedAt: now,
  }

  tasks.push(task)
  saveTasks(data.teamId, tasks)
  return task
}
```

**New:**  
```
export function createTask(data: {
  teamId: string
  subject: string
  description?: string
  assigneeAgentId?: string | null
  blockedBy?: string[]
  priority?: number
}): Promise<Task> {
  return withLock('tasks', () => {
    const tasks = loadTasks(data.teamId)
    const now = new Date().toISOString()

    const task: Task = {
      id: uuidv4(),
      teamId: data.teamId,
      subject: data.subject,
      description: data.description,
      status: 'pending',
      assigneeAgentId: data.assigneeAgentId || null,
      blockedBy: data.blockedBy || [],
      priority: data.priority,
      createdAt: now,
      updatedAt: now,
    }

    tasks.push(task)
    saveTasks(data.teamId, tasks)
    return task
  })
}
```

**Result:**

The file /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/task-registry.ts has been updated successfully.

<summary>🔧 Tool: Edit -- `task-registry.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

**File:** `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/task-registry.ts`  

**Old:**  
```
export function updateTask(
  teamId: string,
  taskId: string,
  updates: Partial<Pick<Task, 'subject' | 'description' | 'status' | 'assigneeAgentId' | 'blockedBy' | 'priority'>>
): { task: Task | null; unblocked: Task[] } {
  const tasks = loadTasks(teamId)
  const index = tasks.findIndex(t => t.id === taskId)
  if (index === -1) return { task: null, unblocked: [] }

  const now = new Date().toISOString()
  const wasCompleted = tasks[index].status === 'completed'
  const isNowCompleted = updates.status === 'completed'

  tasks[index] = {
    ...tasks[index],
    ...updates,
    updatedAt: now,
  }

  // Set timestamps based on status changes
  if ((updates.status === 'in_progress' || updates.status === 'review') && !tasks[index].startedAt) {
    tasks[index].startedAt = now
  }
  if (updates.status === 'completed' && !tasks[index].completedAt) {
    tasks[index].completedAt = now
  }

  // Find newly unblocked tasks when a task is completed
  let unblocked: Task[] = []
  if (!wasCompleted && isNowCompleted) {
    unblocked = tasks.filter(t => {
      if (!t.blockedBy.includes(taskId)) return false
      // Check if ALL blockers are now completed
      return t.blockedBy.every(depId => {
        const dep = tasks.find(d => d.id === depId)
        return dep && dep.status === 'completed'
      })
    })
  }

  saveTasks(teamId, tasks)
  return { task: tasks[index], unblocked }
}
```

**New:**

    const index = tasks.findIndex(t => t.id === taskId)
    if (index === -1) return { task: null, unblocked: [] }

    const now = new Date().toISOString()
    const wasCompleted = tasks[index

```
export function deleteTask(teamId: string, taskId: string): boolean {
  const tasks = loadTasks(teamId)
  const filtered = tasks
    .filter(t => t.id !== taskId)
    .map(t => ({
      ...t,
      blockedBy: t.blockedBy.filter(id => id !== taskId),
    }))

  if (filtered.length === tasks.length) return false
  saveTasks(teamId, filtered)
  return true
}
```

**New:**  
```
export function deleteTask(teamId: string, taskId: string): Promise<boolean> {
  return withLock('tasks', () => {
    const tasks = loadTasks(teamId)
    const filtered = tasks
      .filter(t => t.id !== taskId)
      .map(t => ({
        ...t,
        blockedBy: t.blockedBy.filter(id => id !== taskId),
      }))

    if (filtered.length === tasks.length) return false
    saveTasks(teamId, filtered)
    return true
  })
}
```

   156→    if ((updates.status === 'in_progress' || updates.status === 'review') && !tasks[index].startedAt) {  
   157→      tasks[index].startedAt = now  
   158→    }  
   159→    if (updates.status === 'completed' && !tasks[index].completedAt) {  
   160→      tasks[index].completedAt = now  
   161→    }  
   162→  
   163→    // Find newly unblocked tasks when a task is completed  
   164→    let unblocked: Task[] = []  
   165→    if (!wasCompleted && isNowCompleted) {  
   166→      unblocked = tasks.filter(t => {  
   167→        if (!t.blockedBy.includes(taskId)) return false  
   168→        // Check if ALL blockers are now completed  
   169→        return t.blockedBy.every(depId => {  
   170→          const dep = tasks.find(d => d.id === depId)  
   171→          return dep && dep.status === 'completed'  
   172→        })  
   173→      })  
   174→    }  
   175→  
   176→    saveTasks(teamId, tasks)  
   177→    return { task: tasks[index], unblocked }  
   178→  })  
   179→}  

</details>

   180→  
   181→/**  
   182→ * Delete a task and clean up references in other tasks' blockedBy arrays  
   183→ */  
   184→export function deleteTask(teamId: string, taskId: string): Promise<boolean> {  
   185→  return withLock('tasks', () => {  
   186→    const tasks = loadTasks(teamId)  
   187→    const filtered = tasks  
   188→      .filter(t => t.id !== taskId)  
   189→      .map(t => ({  
   190→        ...t,  
   191→        blockedBy: t.blockedBy.filter(id => id !== taskId),  
   192→      }))  
   193→  
   194→    if (filtered.length === tasks.length) return false  
   195→    saveTasks(teamId, filtered)  
   196→    return true  
   197→  })  
   198→}  
   199→

     1→/**  
     2→ * Team Resource ACL — checks whether an agent (or web UI request)  
     3→ * is allowed to access a given team's resources.  
     4→ *  
     5→ * Open teams (type undefined or 'open') impose no restrictions.  
     6→ * Closed teams restrict access to the manager, chief-of-staff,  
     7→ * and team members only.

    10→import { isManager } from './governance'  
    11→import { getTeam } from './team-registry'  
    12→  
    13→export interface TeamAccessInput {  
    14→  teamId: string  
    15→  requestingAgentId?: string // undefined = web UI request (always allowed)  
    16→}  
    17→  
    18→export interface TeamAccessResult {  
    19→  allowed: boolean  
    20→  reason?: string  
    21→}  
    22→  
    23→/**  
    24→ * Determine whether the requester may access the team's resources.  
    25→ *  
    26→ * Decision order:  
    27→ *  1. Web UI (no agentId)      → allowed  
    28→ *  2. Team not found           → allowed (caller handles 404)  
    29→ *  3. Team is open / untyped   → allowed  
    30→ *  4. Requester is MANAGER     → allowed  
    31→ *  5. Requester is chief-of-staff → allowed  
    32→ *  6. Requester is a member    → allowed  
    33→ *  7. Otherwise                → denied  
    34→ */  
    35→export function checkTeamAccess(input: TeamAccessInput): TeamAccessResult {  
    36→  // 1. Web UI requests (no X-Agent-Id header) always pass  
    37→  if (input.requestingAgentId === undefined) {  
    38→    return { allowed: true }  
    39→  }  
    40→  
    41→  // 2. Team not found — let the caller deal with 404  
    42→  const team = getTeam(input.teamId)  
    43→  if (!team) {  
    44→    return { allowed: true }  
    45→  }  
    46→  
    47→  // 3. Open teams (or teams with no explicit type) have no ACL  
    48→  if (team.type !== 'closed') {  
    49→    return { allowed: true }  
    50→  }  
    51→  
    52→  // 4. MANAGER role always has access  
    53→  if (isManager(input.requestingAgentId)) {  
    54→    return { allowed: true }  
    55→  }  
    56→  
    57→  // 5.

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-17 00:23:40]*

<summary>🔧 Tool: Read -- `file-lock.ts`</summary>

  "file_path": "/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/file-lock.ts"
}
```

**Result:**

     1→/**  
     2→ * File Lock — in-process mutex for serializing load→modify→save operations  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Prevents concurrent read-modify-write races within a single Node.js process.  
     5→ * Each registry file gets its own named lock. When one API request is mid-write,  
     6→ * other requests for the same file queue up and run sequentially.  
     7→ *  
     8→ * This is sufficient for Phase 1 (single Next.js process, localhost).  
     9→ * For multi-process deployments, replace with advisory file locks (e.g., proper-lockfile).  
    10→ */  
    11→  
    12→// Map of lock name -> queue of pending resolve callbacks  
    13→const locks = new Map<string, Array<() => void>>()  
    14→// Set of currently held lock names  
    15→const held = new Set<string>()  
    16→  
    17→/**  
    18→ * Acquire a named lock. Returns a release function.  
    19→ * If the lock is already held, the caller awaits until it is released.  
    20→ */  
    21→export function acquireLock(name: string): Promise<() => void> {  
    22→  if (!held.has(name)) {  
    23→    // Lock is free — acquire immediately  
    24→    held.add(name)  
    25→    return Promise.resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    26→  }  
    27→  
    28→  // Lock is held — enqueue and wait  
    29→  return new Promise<() => void>((resolve) => {  
    30→    if (!locks.has(name)) {  
    31→      locks.set(name, [])  
    32→    }  
    33→    locks.get(name)!.push(() => {  
    34→      resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    35→    })  
    36→  })  
    37→}  
    38→  
    39→/**  
    40→ * Release a named lock and wake the next waiter if any.  
    41→ */  
    42→function releaseLock(name: string): void {  
    43→  const queue = locks.get(name)  
    44→  if (queue && queue.length > 0) {  
    45→    // Hand lock to next waiter (don't remove from held set)  
    46→    const next = queue.shift()!  
    47→    if (queue.length === 0) {  
    48→      locks.delete(name)  
    49→    }  
    50→    next()  
    51→  } else {  
    52→    // No waiters — release the lock  
    53→    hel  

... [473 more chars truncated]  

</details>

    54→  
    55→/** Set governance password (bcrypt hash with 12 salt rounds) */  
    56→export async function setPassword(plaintext: string): Promise<void> {  
    57→  return withLock('governance', () => {  
    58→    const config = loadGovernance()  
    59→    config.passwordHash = bcrypt.hashSync(plaintext, BCRYPT_SALT_ROUNDS)

    63→}  
    64→  
    65→/** Verify plaintext against stored password hash. Returns false if no password set. */  
    66→export function verifyPassword(plaintext: string): boolean {  
    67→  const config = loadGovernance()  
    68→  if (!config.passwordHash) {  
    69→    return false  
    70→  }  
    71→  return bcrypt.compareSync(plaintext, config.passwordHash)  
    72→}  
    73→  
    74→/** Get the current manager agent ID, or null if none set */  
    75→export function getManagerId(): string | null {  
    76→  const config = loadGovernance()  
    77→  return config.managerId  
    78→}  
    79→  
    80→/** Set the manager agent ID and persist */  
    81→export async function setManager(agentId: string): Promise<void> {  
    82→  return withLock('governance', () => {  
    83→    const config = loadGovernance()  
    84→    config.managerId = agentId  
    85→    saveGovernance(config)  
    86→  })  
    87→}  
    88→  
    89→/** Remove the manager (set to null) and persist */  
    90→export async function removeManager(): Promise<void> {  
    91→  return withLock('governance', () => {  
    92→    const config = loadGovernance()  
    93→    config.managerId = null  
    94→    saveGovernance(config)  
    95→  })  
    96→}  
    97→  
    98→/** Check if agentId is the singleton manager */  
    99→export function isManager(agentId: string): boolean {  

</details>

     1→/**  
     2→ * Message Filter — enforces closed-team messaging isolation  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Determines whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed  
     5→ * based on governance roles (MANAGER, Chief-of-Staff) and closed-team  
     6→ * membership. Open-world agents (not in any closed team) can message  
     7→ * freely unless the recipient is inside a closed team.  
     8→ */  
     9→  
    10→import { loadGovernance } from './governance'  
    11→import { loadTeams } from './team-registry'  
    12→  
    13→export interface MessageFilterInput {  
    14→  senderAgentId: string | null // null = mesh-forwarded message  
    15→  recipientAgentId: string  
    16→}  
    17→  
    18→export interface MessageFilterResult {  
    19→  allowed: boolean  
    20→  reason?: string  
    21→}  
    22→  
    23→/**  
    24→ * Check whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed.  
    25→ *  
    26→ * Algorithm (R6.1–R6.7):  
    27→ * 1. Mesh-forwarded (senderAgentId null): always allowed (trust mesh peers)  
    28→ * 2. Neither in a closed team: allowed (open world, current behavior) (R6.4)  
    29→ * 3. Sender is MANAGER: always allowed (R6.3)  
    30→ * 4. Sender is COS of any closed team: can reach MANAGER, other COS, own team members (R6.2)  
    31→ * 5. Normal closed-team member: can reach same-team members and own COS (R6.1)  
    32→ * 6. Outside sender to closed-team recipient: denied (R6.5)  
    33→ * 7. Default: allowed  
    34→ *  
    35→ * IMPORTANT (R6.7): Uses getClosedTeamsForAgent (plural) to correctly handle  
    36→ * COS agents who belong to multiple closed teams simultaneously.  
    37→ */  
    38→export function checkMessageAllowed(input: MessageFilterInput): MessageFilterResult {  
    39→  const { senderAgentId, recipientAgentId } = input  
    40→  
    41→  // Step 1: Mesh-forwarded messages are always trusted  
    42→  if (senderAgentId === null) {  
    43→    return { allowed: true }  
    44→  }  
    45→  
    46→  // Single snapshot of all state — avoids redundant file reads from   

... [173 more chars truncated]

    51→  const closedTeams = teams.filter(t => t.type === 'closed')

    62→  // Step 2: Neither party is in a closed team — open world, allow freely (R6.4)

    72→  // Step 4: Sender is Chief-of-Staff of some closed team (R6.2)

    76→      return { allowed: true }  
    77→    }  
    78→    // COS-to-COS bridge: any COS can message any other COS  
    79→    if (agentIsCOS(recipientAgentId)) {  
    80→      return { allowed: true }  
    81→    }  
    82→    // COS can message members of ANY of their closed teams (R6.7 — plural, not singular)  
    83→    if (senderTeams.some(team => team.agentIds.includes(recipientAgentId))) {  
    84→      return { allowed: true }  
    85→    }  
    86→    return {  
    87→      allowed: false,  
    88→      reason: 'Chief-of-Staff can only message MANAGER, other Chiefs-of-Staff, and own team members',  
    89→    }  
    90→  }

    92→  // Step 5: Sender is a normal member of

     1→import { NextRequest, NextResponse } from 'next/server'  
     2→import { loadGovernance, setPassword, verifyPassword } from '@/lib/governance'  
     3→  
     4→export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {  
     5→  try {  
     6→    const body = await request.json()  
     7→    const { password, currentPassword } = body  
     8→  
     9→    if (!password || typeof password !== 'string' || password.length < 6) {  
    10→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Password must be at least 6 characters' }, { status: 400 })  
    11→    }  
    12→  
    13→    const config = loadGovernance()  
    14→  
    15→    // If password already set, require current password  
    16→    if (config.passwordHash) {  
    17→      if (!currentPassword || !verifyPassword(currentPassword)) {  
    18→        return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Invalid current password' }, { status: 401 })  
    19→      }  
    20→    }  
    21→  
    22→    const isChange = !!config.passwordHash  
    23→    await setPassword(password)  
    24→  
    25→    if (isChange) {  
    26→      console.log('[governance] Password changed at', new Date().toISOString())  
    27→    } else {  
    28→      console.log('[governance] Password set at', new Date().toISOString())  
    29→    }  
    30→  
    31→    return NextResponse.json({ success: true })  
    32→  } catch (error) {  
    33→    console.error('Failed to set password:', error)  
    34→    return NextResponse.json(  
    35→      { error: error instanceof Error ? error.message : 'Failed to set password' },  
    36→      { status: 500 }  
    37→    )  
    38→  }  
    39→}

     1→import { NextRequest, NextResponse } from 'next/server'  
     2→import { checkMessageAllowed } from '@/lib/message-filter'  
     3→import { loadAgents } from '@/lib/agent-registry'  
     4→  
     5→// In-memory cache: avoids re-reading governance + teams files for every agent  
     6→// on each request. TTL of 5 seconds balances freshness with performance.  
     7→const cache = new Map<string, { ids: string[]; expiresAt: number }>()  
     8→const CACHE_TTL_MS = 5_000  
     9→  
    10→export async function GET(request: NextRequest) {  
    11→  try {  
    12→    const agentId = request.nextUrl.searchParams.get('agentId')  
    13→  
    14→    if (!agentId) {  
    15→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'agentId query parameter is required' }, { status: 400 })  
    16→    }  
    17→  
    18→    // Check cache first  
    19→    const cached = cache.get(agentId)  
    20→    if (cached && Date.now() < cached.expiresAt) {  
    21→      return NextResponse.json({ reachableAgentIds: cached.ids })  
    22→    }  
    23→  
    24→    // Cache miss or expired — compute reachable agents  
    25→    const allAgents = loadAgents()  
    26→    const reachableAgentIds: string[] = []  
    27→  
    28→    for (const agent of allAgents) {  
    29→      if (agent.id === agentId) continue  
    30→      if (agent.deletedAt) continue  
    31→  
    32→      const result = checkMessageAllowed({  
    33→        senderAgentId: agentId,  
    34→        recipientAgentId: agent.id,  
    35→      })  
    36→  
    37→      if (result.allowed) {  
    38→        reachableAgentIds.push(agent.id)  
    39→      }  
    40→    }  
    41→  
    42→    // Store in cache with TTL  
    43→    cache.set(agentId, { ids: reachableAgentIds, expiresAt: Date.now() + CACHE_TTL_MS })  
    44→  
    45→    // Evict stale/expired entries on every cache write to prevent unbounded growth  
    46→    const now = Date.now()  
    47→    for (const [key, entry] of cache) {  
    48→      if (now >= entry.expiresAt) cache.delete(key)  
    49→    }  
    50→  
    51→    r

    55→  
    56→    // Validate source and destination are different teams (R5.6)  
    57→    if (fromTeamId === toTeamId) {  
    58→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Source and destination teams must be different' }, { status: 400 })  
    59→    }  
    60→  
    61→    // Verify the agent is actually in the fromTeam  
    62→    const teams = loadTeams()  
    63→    const fromTeam = teams.find(t => t.id === fromTeamId)  
    64→    if (!fromTeam) {  
    65→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Source team not found' }, { status: 404 })  
    66→    }  
    67→    if (!fromTeam.agentIds.includes(agentId)) {  
    68→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Agent is not in the source team' }, { status: 400 })  
    69→    }  
    70→  
    71→    // Validate destination team exists (R5.5)  
    72→    const toTeam = teams.find(t => t.id === toTeamId)  
    73→    if (!toTeam) {  
    74→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Destination team not found' }, { status: 404 })  
    75→    }  
    76→  
    77→    // COS cannot be transferred out of their own team — would orphan the team (R5.4)  
    78→    if (fromTeam.chiefOfStaffId === agentId) {  
    79→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Cannot transfer the Chief-of-Staff out of their team — remove COS role first' }, { status: 400 })  
    80→    }  
    81→  
    82→    // Check if source team is closed (transfer approval only needed for closed teams)  
    83→    if (fromTeam.type !== 'closed') {  
    84→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Transfer requests are only needed for closed teams. Use direct team update for open teams.' }, { status: 400 })  
    85→    }  
    86→  
    87→    // Check for duplicate pending requests  
    88→    const pending = getPe

     1→# Code Correctness Report: types-and-lib

     7→  
     8→## MUST-FIX  
     9→  
    10→### [CC-001] task-registry.ts: No file locking on write operations — race condition  
    11→- **File:** /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/task-registry.ts:95,132,179  
    12→- **Severity:** MUST-FIX  
    13→- **Category:** race-condition  
    14→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    15→- **Description:** `createTask()`, `updateTask()`, and `deleteTask()` all perform read-modify-write sequences (`loadTasks` -> mutate -> `saveTasks`) without any file locking. Unlike `team-registry.ts`, `transfer-registry.ts`, and `governance.ts`, which all use `withLock()` from `@/lib/file-lock`, `task-registry.ts` does not import or use `withLock` at all. Two concurrent API requests to create/update/delete tasks on the same team will race: both read the same file, mutate independently, and the second write silently overwrites the first, losing data.  
    16→- **Evidence:**  
    17→  ```typescript  
    18→  // lib/task-registry.ts — NO withLock anywhere in this file  
    19→  export function createTask(data: { teamId: string; ... }): Task {  
    20→    const tasks = loadTasks(data.teamId)  // READ  
    21→    // ... build task ...  
    22→    tasks.push(task)                       // MUTATE  
    23→    saveTasks(data.teamId, tasks)          // WRITE — can overwrite concurrent changes  
    24→    return task  
    25→  }  
    26→  ```  
    27→  Compare with `team-registry.ts` which wraps every write in `withLock('teams', () => { ... })`.  
    28→- **Fix:** Import `withLock` from `@/lib/file-lock` and wrap `createTask`, `updateTask`, and `deleteTask` in `withLock('tasks-' + teamId, ...)`. This requires making them `async` (matching the pattern in `team-registry.ts`). Note: `wouldCreateCycle` is read-only and does not need locking.  
    29→  
    30→## SHOULD-FIX  
    31→  

... [10731 more chars truncated]  

</details>

    11→- **File:** /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/app/api/agents/[id]/transfer/route.ts:33  
    12→- **Severity:** MUST-FIX  
    13→- **Category:** type-safety  
    14→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    15→- **Description:** The route handler uses `{ params }: { params: { id: string } }` and accesses `params.id` synchronously at line 37. Every other `[id]` route in this codebase (40+ occurrences) uses `{ params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string }> }` with `const { id } = await params`. This project runs Next.js 14.2.35 where params is a Promise in App Router route handlers. Synchronous access works today because Next.js resolves it internally, but it emits a deprecation warning and will break in Next.js 15.  
    16→- **Evidence:**  
    17→  ```typescript  
    18→  // Line 31-37 of transfer/route.ts  
    19→  export async function POST(  
    20→    request: Request,

    22→  ) {  
    23→    try {  
    24→      let agent = getAgent(params.id)  // <-- synchronous access  
    25→  ```  
    26→  vs. all other routes:  
    27→  ```typescript  
    28→  // Example from resolve/route.ts line 14-19  
    29→  export async function POST(  
    30→    request: NextRequest,  
    31→    { params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string }> }  // <-- Promise  
    32→  ) {  
    33→    const { id } = await params  // <-- awaited  
    34→  ```  
    35→- **Fix:** Change type to `Promise<{ id: string }>` and add `const { id } = await params` at the top of the function. Also change `Request` to `NextRequest` for consistency.

    16→- **Severity:** SHOULD-FIX

    18→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    19→- **Description:** The `refresh` callback fires three parallel fetches and unconditionally writes results to state. If `agentId` changes while fetches are in-flight (e.g., user clicks between agents quickly), the older fetch's `.then()` handler will overwrite state with data that no longer matches the current `agentId`. Because `refresh` is re-created via `useCallback([agentId])`, the old closure's `setLoading`/`setAllTeams`/etc. still reference the same state setters. There is no cancellation (AbortController) and no staleness guard (e.g., checking a ref against current agentId before calling setState).

    34→        setPendingTransfers(transfersData.requests ?? [])  
    35→      })  
    36→      ...

    38→  ```

  3600→+  if (queue && queue.length > 0) {  
  3601→+    // Hand lock to next waiter (don't remove from held set)  
  3602→+    const next = queue.shift()!  
  3603→+    if (queue.length === 0) {  
  3604→+      locks.delete(name)  
  3605→+    }  
  3606→+    next()  
  3607→+  } else {  
  3608→+    // No waiters — release the lock  
  3609→+    held.delete(name)  
  3610→+    locks.delete(name)  
  3611→+  }  
  3612→+}  
  3613→+  
  3614→+/**  
  3615→+ * Run a function under a named lock.  
  3616→+ * Convenience wrapper: acquires, runs fn, releases (even on error).  
  3617→+ */  
  3618→+export async function withLock<T>(name: string, fn: () => T | Promise<T>): Promise<T> {  
  3619→+  const release = await acquireLock(name)  
  3620→+  try {  
  3621→+    return await fn()  
  3622→+  } finally {  
  3623→+    release()  
  3624→+  }  
  3625→+}

    10→### [CC-001] task-registry.ts: No file locking on write operations — race condition  
    11→- **File:** /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/task-registry.ts:95,132,179  
    12→- **Severity:** MUST-FIX  
    13→- **Category:** race-condition  
    14→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    15→- **Description:** `createTask()`, `updateTask()`, and `deleteTask()` all perform read-modify-write sequences (`loadTasks` -> mutate -> `saveTasks`) without any file locking. Unlike `team-registry.ts`, `transfer-registry.ts`, and `governance.ts`, which all use `withLock()` from `@/lib/file-lock`, `task-registry.ts` does not import or use `withLock` at all. Two concurrent API requests to create/update/delete tasks on the same team will race: both read the same file, mutate independently, and the second write silently overwrites the first, losing data.  
    16→- **Evidence:**  
    17→  ```typescript  
    18→  // lib/task-registry.ts — NO withLock anywhere in this file  
    19→  export function createTask(data: { teamId: string; ... }): Task {  
    20→    const tasks = loadTasks(data.teamId)  // READ  
    21→    // ... build task ...  
    22→    tasks.push(task)                       // MUTATE  
    23→    saveTasks(data.teamId, tasks)          // WRITE — can overwrite concurrent changes  
    24→    return task  
    25→  }  
    26→  ```  
    27→  Compare with `team-registry.ts` which wraps every write in `withLock('teams', () => { ... })`.  
    28→- **Fix:** Import `withLock` from `@/lib/file-lock` and wrap `createTask`, `updateTask`, and `deleteTask` in `withLock('tasks-' + teamId, ...)`. This requires making them `async` (matching the pattern in `team-registry.ts`). Note: `wouldCreateCycle` is read-only and does not need locking.  
    29→  
    30→## SHOULD-FIX  
    31→  

... [10731 more chars truncated]

    22→  ) {  
    23→    try {  
    24→      let agent = getAgent(params.id)  // <-- synchronous access  
    25→  ```  
    26→  vs. all other routes:  
    27→  ```typescript  
    28→  // Example from resolve/route.ts line 14-19  
    29→  export async function POST(  
    30→    request: NextRequest,  
    31→    { params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string }> }  // <-- Promise  
    32→  ) {  
    33→    const { id } = await params  // <-- awaited  
    34→  ```  
    35→- **Fix:** Change type to `Promise<{ id: string }>` and add `const { id } = await params` at the top of the function. Also change `Request` to `NextRequest` for consistency.

Changes needed:  

1. **SHOULD-FIX: COS guard ordering in removeAgentFromTeam**: Find the `removeAgentFromTeam` function. The COS guard check (`if (team.chiefOfStaffId === targetAgentId)`) currently runs AFTER the filter computation (`updatedAgentIds = team.agentIds.filter(...)`). Move the COS guard check BEFORE the filter. The pattern should be:  
```typescript
// Check COS guard BEFORE computing the update
if (team.chiefOfStaffId === targetAgentId) {
  return { success: false, error: 'Cannot remove the Chief-of-Staff...' }
}
const updatedAgentIds = team.agentIds.filter((id: string) => id !== targetAgentId)
```

2. **SHOULD-FIX: addAgentToTeam HTTP race**: In `addAgentToTeam`, add a comment explaining the known limitation:  
```typescript
// Note: This performs a client-side read-modify-write across two HTTP requests.
// Concurrent modifications from multiple tabs may lose updates.
// Server-side withLock protects file integrity but not HTTP-level atomicity.
// Acceptable for Phase 1 (single user, localhost). TODO: atomic endpoint for Phase 2.
```

3. **Error handling on fetches**: In `addAgentToTeam` and `removeAgentFromTeam`, after the initial GET fetch (e.g., `fetch('/api/teams/${teamId}')`), check `.ok` before `.json()`:  
```typescript
if (!r.ok) throw new Error('Failed to fetch team')
```
Same for the PUT response — check .ok.

## <span style="color:#2196F3">◆ USER</span>  *[2026-02-17 00:41:50]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #2196F3; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Fix lib/message-filter.ts for COS-not-in-agentIds blind spot.  

Read the file first: /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/message-filter.ts  

The issue: senderTeams is derived from `closedTeams.filter(t => t.agentIds.includes(senderAgentId))`. If a COS is in chiefOfStaffId but NOT in agentIds (data corruption edge case), senderTeams will be empty. The COS can reach MANAGER and other COS, but NOT their own team members via the same-team check.  

Fix: In step 4 (COS bridge / same-team check), also derive COS teams from chiefOfStaffId. Specifically:  

After computing `senderTeams`, add:  
```typescript
// Also include teams where sender is COS (defense against COS not in agentIds)
const senderCosTeams = closedTeams.filter(t => t.chiefOfStaffId === senderAgentId)
const allSenderTeams = [...new Set([...senderTeams.map(t => t.id), ...senderCosTeams.map(t => t.id)])]
```

Then in the same-team check (step 4), use `allSenderTeams` to also check COS team membership:  
```typescript
// Check if any of sender's teams (by membership OR COS role) include the recipient
const senderTeamMembers = closedTeams
  .filter(t => allSenderTeams.includes(t.id))
  .flatMap(t => t.agentIds)
```

Keep the existing logic intact, just augment the senderTeams derivation. Add a comment explaining the defense-in-depth.  

REPORTING RULES:  
- Return to orchestrator ONLY: "[DONE/FAILED] task - brief result"  
- Max 2 lines back to orchestrator

     1→/**  
     2→ * Message Filter — enforces closed-team messaging isolation  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Determines whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed  
     5→ * based on governance roles (MANAGER, Chief-of-Staff) and closed-team  
     6→ * membership. Open-world agents (not in any closed team) can message  
     7→ * freely unless the recipient is inside a closed team.  
     8→ */  
     9→  
    10→import { loadGovernance } from './governance'  
    11→import { loadTeams } from './team-registry'  
    12→  
    13→export interface MessageFilterInput {  
    14→  senderAgentId: string | null // null = mesh-forwarded message  
    15→  recipientAgentId: string  
    16→}  
    17→  
    18→export interface MessageFilterResult {  
    19→  allowed: boolean  
    20→  reason?: string  
    21→}  
    22→  
    23→/**  
    24→ * Check whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed.  
    25→ *  
    26→ * Algorithm (R6.1–R6.7):  
    27→ * 1. Mesh-forwarded (senderAgentId null): always allowed (trust mesh peers)  
    28→ * 2. Neither in a closed team: allowed (open world, current behavior) (R6.4)  
    29→ * 3. Sender is MANAGER: always allowed (R6.3)  
    30→ * 4. Sender is COS of any closed team: can reach MANAGER, other COS, own team members (R6.2)  
    31→ * 5. Normal closed-team member: can reach same-team members and own COS (R6.1)  
    32→ * 6. Outside sender to closed-team recipient: denied (R6.5)  
    33→ * 7. Default: allowed  
    34→ *  
    35→ * IMPORTANT (R6.7): Uses getClosedTeamsForAgent (plural) to correctly handle  
    36→ * COS agents who belong to multiple closed teams simultaneously.  
    37→ */  
    38→export function checkMessageAllowed(input: MessageFilterInput): MessageFilterResult {  
    39→  const { senderAgentId, recipientAgentId } = input  
    40→  
    41→  // Step 1: Mesh-forwarded messages are always trusted  
    42→  if (senderAgentId === null) {  
    43→    return { allowed: true }  
    44→  }  
    45→  
    46→  // Single snapshot of all state — avoids redundant file reads from

    51→  const closedTeams = teams.filter(t => t.type === 'closed')

    53→  const recipientTeams = closedTeams.filter(t => t.agentIds.includes(recipientAgentId))

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-17 00:42:25]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I can see the issue clearly. On line 52, `senderTeams` only checks `agentIds.includes(senderAgentId)`. If a COS is listed as `chiefOfStaffId` but NOT in `agentIds`, line 83's same-team check will fail. I also need to fix `senderInClosed` on line 54, because a COS who's not in `agentIds` would be treated as not in a closed team, which would skip step 4 entirely and fall through to step 6 (denied).  

Wait -- actually, step 4 checks `agentIsCOS(senderAgentId)` which uses `chiefOfStaffId`, so if the COS is not in `agentIds`, `senderInClosed` is false, step 2 checks both parties... Let me trace carefully:  

- If COS is not in `agentIds` but is `chiefOfStaffId`, `senderInClosed = false`  
- If recipient IS in a closed team, `recipientInClosed = true`  
- Step 2: `!senderInClosed && !recipientInClosed` = false (recipient is in closed), so we continue  
- Step 3: manager check, skip if not manager  
- Step 4: `agentIsCOS(senderAgentId)` = true (checks `chiefOfStaffId`), so we enter step 4  
- Line 83: `senderTeams.some(...)` -- but `senderTeams` is empty! So this returns false.  
- Falls through to the denial on line 86-89.  

So the COS can reach MANAGER and other COS but NOT their own team members. This confirms the bug. The fix needs to augment `senderTeams` derivation and the check on line 83.  

</div>

**New:**  
```
  // Derive closed-team membership from the single snapshot
  const closedTeams = teams.filter(t => t.type === 'closed')
  const senderTeams = closedTeams.filter(t => t.agentIds.includes(senderAgentId))
  const recipientTeams = closedTeams.filter(t => t.agentIds.includes(recipientAgentId))
  // Defense-in-depth: also include teams where sender is COS via chiefOfStaffId,
  // in case COS was not added to agentIds (data corruption edge case).
  const senderCosTeams = closedTeams.filter(t => t.chiefOfStaffId === senderAgentId)
  const allSenderTeamIds = [...new Set([...senderTeams.map(t => t.id), ...senderCosTeams.map(t => t.id)])]
  const senderInClosed = senderTeams.length > 0 || senderCosTeams.length > 0
  const recipientInClosed = recipientTeams.length > 0
```

**New:**  
```
    // COS can message members of ANY of their closed teams (R6.7 — plural, not singular)
    // Uses allSenderTeamIds to cover COS-not-in-agentIds edge case
    const cosTeamMembers = closedTeams
      .filter(t => allSenderTeamIds.includes(t.id))
      .flatMap(t => t.agentIds)
    if (cosTeamMembers.includes(recipientAgentId)) {
      return { allowed: true }
    }
```

## <span style="color:#2196F3">◆ USER</span>  *[2026-02-17 00:41:50]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #2196F3; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Fix lib/governance.ts for timing side-channel in verifyPassword.  

Read the file first: /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/governance.ts  

The issue: verifyPassword() returns false immediately when no password hash is set, creating a timing difference that reveals whether governance has a password.  

Fix: When no hash is set, run a dummy bcrypt comparison against a static hash so the timing is consistent:  

```typescript
export function verifyPassword(password: string): boolean {
  const config = loadGovernance()
  if (!config.passwordHash) {
    // Constant-time defense: run bcrypt even when no password is set
    // to prevent timing side-channel that reveals password existence
    bcrypt.compareSync(password, '$2a$12$000000000000000000000000000000000000000000')
    return false
  }
  return bcrypt.compareSync(password, config.passwordHash)
}
```

Use a valid bcrypt hash format for the dummy (any static bcrypt hash will do). Add a comment explaining why.  

REPORTING RULES:  
- Return to orchestrator ONLY: "[DONE/FAILED] task - brief result"  
- Max 2 lines back to orchestrator  


</div>

Fix scripts/remote-install.sh for literal \n in gw_list.  

Read the file first: /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/scripts/remote-install.sh  

This is a large file (~1300 lines). Search for `gw_list` to find the relevant section.  

The issue: The gw_list variable is built using `\n` inside double-quoted strings, which produces literal `\n` characters on macOS instead of actual newlines.  

Fix: Change the gw_list concatenation to use `$'\n'` for real newlines. For example, change:  
```bash
gw_list="${gw_list}\n- ${gw_display}"
```
to:  
```bash
gw_list="${gw_list}"$'\n'"- ${gw_display}"
```

Or use printf: `gw_list=$(printf '%s\n- %s' "$gw_list" "$gw_display")`  

Apply this to ALL occurrences of gw_list that use `\n`.  

REPORTING RULES:  
- Return to orchestrator ONLY: "[DONE/FAILED] task - brief result"  
- Max 2 lines back to orchestrator

2. Line 1230 passes `gw_list` to `sed` -- even with real newlines, sed would have trouble with literal newlines in the replacement string on macOS.

The best portable approach is to use `printf` to build the list, then use `awk` for substitution, or escape newlines for sed. Let me use a simpler approach: build with real newlines, then use `awk` for the substitution.  

Actually, the simplest fix that's portable: use `printf '%s\n'` to build the list, then replace using a temp-file approach or perl. But let me keep it minimal. I'll use `$'\n'` for building, and then for the sed substitution, I'll replace it with a perl one-liner since sed can't handle newlines in replacement on macOS.

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-17 00:42:17]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Edit -- `remote-install.sh`</summary>

**Input:**

**File:** `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/scripts/remote-install.sh`  

**Old:**  
```
            # Use perl for substitution since sed cannot handle real newlines in replacement on macOS
            perl -i -pe "s|\\{\\{ACTIVE_GATEWAYS_LIST\\}\\}|${gw_list}|g" "$MAILMAN_DIR/CLAUDE.md"
```

**New:**  
```
            # Use awk for substitution since sed cannot handle real newlines in replacement on macOS
            GW_LIST="$gw_list" awk '{
                gsub(/\{\{ACTIVE_GATEWAYS_LIST\}\}/, ENVIRON["GW_LIST"])
                print
            }' "$MAILMAN_DIR/CLAUDE.md" > "$MAILMAN_DIR/CLAUDE.md.tmp" && mv "$MAILMAN_DIR/CLAUDE.md.tmp" "$MAILMAN_DIR/CLAUDE.md"
```
